    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_77757184" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/77757184" />
    <a title="Morgan F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f"><img alt="Morgan F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1262298598p2/2941288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/77757184?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Morgan F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Morgan F" href="/user/show/2941288-morgan-f">Morgan F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=2000s">2000s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=otis-library">otis-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=pretty-covers">pretty-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=memory">memory</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=read-2011">read-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=medium-sized">medium-sized</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=dystopian-apocalyptic">dystopian-apocalyptic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=amnesia">amnesia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2941288-morgan-f?shelf=self-perception">self-perception</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer77757184" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2355471686061223436">I've been waiting to read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1902241.The_Adoration_of_Jenna_Fox' title='The Adoration of Jenna Fox by Mary E. Pearson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Adoration of Jenna Fox</a> for four years, ever since I happened upon it while browsing in B&N. I bypassed it, but every time I saw that novel from then on I would say to myself "I'm going to read you one day" (I said it in a Southern accent too, but thats irrelevant). Well, I finally did. All that hype, four years worth, and I am not disappointed in the least, as a matter of fact. <br/><br/>Jenna Fox is a 17-year old girl who has just woken up after an 18 month coma. She doesn't</span>
  <span id="freeText2355471686061223436" style="display:none">I've been waiting to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1902241.The_Adoration_of_Jenna_Fox" title="The Adoration of Jenna Fox by Mary E. Pearson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Adoration of Jenna Fox</a> for four years, ever since I happened upon it while browsing in B&amp;N. I bypassed it, but every time I saw that novel from then on I would say to myself "I'm going to read you one day" (I said it in a Southern accent too, but thats irrelevant). Well, I finally did. All that hype, four years worth, and I am not disappointed in the least, as a matter of fact. <br /><br />Jenna Fox is a 17-year old girl who has just woken up after an 18 month coma. She doesn't remember anything, not her parents, herself, even some simple words are completely foreign to her. It's not long before Jenna starts putting together the pieces of what happened to her doing her lost year and a half, and what she reassembles makes her question if she really <i>is</i> Jenna Fox at all. <br /><br />I loved this book. It's speculative and self-reflective, and although the "mystery" of the story isn't too difficult to piece together, the book focuses more on the questions that arise from the conclusion. Don't let the presence of scientific elements discourage you from reading it, the technicality of it is soft, and serves only as backgrounds for the moral questions of the story. <br /><br />Jenna is good protagonist. Never stereotypical, never one-dimensional, she is actually curious, intelligent, and emotional. I could both relate to and understand her emotions, even though her situation was so far from anything in my own life. Some times she understands more than the reader, and sometimes the reader understands more than her. It's a nice balance, and the writing, lyrical and circular, complements her voice perfectly. I loved Jenna and I loved the writing. Although I didn't quite feel for them as completely, Jenna's parents and grandmother also had a spark that made them breathe off the page. They weren't perfect beings, but they were human beings. <br /><br />This novel truly made me think. It provided not with blind entertainment but with earnest questions. My favorite line from the book: "<i>These thoughts are mine alone and no one else's. They exist no where else in the universe but within me.</i>" How do you go about thinking about that? I'll be considering that for days...<br /><br />The reasons why this novel did not receive five stars? Well, there were a few. The weakest parts for me is when I felt Pearson was trying to hard to conventionalize the novel. Like the romance between Jenna and Ethan. The book would have been better without it, but Pearson probably added it in an attempt to draw in readers who are all about the "hawt guys" and "twu luv". Another unnecessary addition was Dane. He was added just to provide an antagonist and a definite bad guy. The novel didn't need an antagonist. The doubt alone in Jenna's mind was conflict enough. Also, the epilogue was sucky and I felt it undermined the message of the story. I turned what I <i>thought</i> was the last page all content and dazed, but then I noticed the 260 years later.....grrrr. So that's it? Every thing is happy? They get to live forever with no consequences? Isn't the whole point of the book is that there ARE CONSEQUENCES???<br /><br />Anyway, this was a great book, somewhere in between <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/764347.Unwind__Unwind___1_" title="Unwind (Unwind, #1) by Neal Shusterman" rel="nofollow noopener">Unwind</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6334.Never_Let_Me_Go" title="Never Let Me Go by Kazuo Ishiguro" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Let Me Go</a> in terms of bio-ethical speculative fiction. It doesn't have the action-y, more commercialized vibe of Unwind, yet it isn't quite as introspective and thoughtful as Never Let Me go. It's somewhere in the middle. <br /><br />Overall, awesome-sauce. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2355471686061223436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_137761692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137761692" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137761692?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137761692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7070751043654636737"><i>The Adoration of Jenna Fox</i> is a simply written story containing many complex issues. Seventeen-year-old Jenna Fox awakens after an eighteen-month coma unaware of who she is - until the woman who claims to be her mother tells her her name. The memories of her life slowly come back to her, filling in the empty crevices of her mind with stories of happiness and friendship. The question is: who is Jenna Fox now? She has her parents, with her mom acting surreptitiously careful, and her dad with his f</span>
  <span id="freeText7070751043654636737" style="display:none"><i>The Adoration of Jenna Fox</i> is a simply written story containing many complex issues. Seventeen-year-old Jenna Fox awakens after an eighteen-month coma unaware of who she is - until the woman who claims to be her mother tells her her name. The memories of her life slowly come back to her, filling in the empty crevices of her mind with stories of happiness and friendship. The question is: who is Jenna Fox now? She has her parents, with her mom acting surreptitiously careful, and her dad with his fake smile. She sees her grandmother, but her grandmother doesn't see her in the same way. Also, she begins to make friends at the local charter school. So how come she isn't feeling 100% right with things as they are?<br /><br />It is difficult to write a summary of this book without giving things away, because Mary Pearson utilizes foreshadowing as a major plot device. As much as I guessed the twists and turns of the novel, I was never exactly accurate, which was a good thing because it always kept me wondering what would happen next.<br /><br />The best thing about this book was how it made me question our society's use of science and medicine. What is the limit when it comes to saving lives? Should we be allowed to extend the natural human lifespan by using artificial means? Most importantly, what makes someone human? <br /><br /><i>The Adoration of Jenna Fox</i> is a thoughtful story that will make readers ponder and question topics of humanity today.<br /><br />Want to read more of my reviews? Follow me <a href="http://thequietvoice18.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2452488935540093111">These thoughts are mine and no one else's. They exist nowhere else in the universe but within me. <br/>When is a cell finally to small to hold our essence?<br/><br/>These are just a few of the musings of the adored Jenna Fox. I personally loved the "gray" pages and think that they beautifully represent the most inner workings of the human mind.<br/><br/>Don't read to much about this book though.   <span id="freeText2452488935540093111" style="display:none">These thoughts are mine and no one else's. They exist nowhere else in the universe but within me. <br />When is a cell finally to small to hold our essence?<br /><br />These are just a few of the musings of the adored Jenna Fox. I personally loved the "gray" pages and think that they beautifully represent the most inner workings of the human mind.<br /><br />Don't read to much about this book though. It is so much better to have no idea what's coming in the storyline. I love books like this where you never would have guessed what's going to happen.<br /><br />When I first heard about this book, I judged it by it's title. I thought "Here we go again. Another book about a teenager who complains about their perfect life." I was so wrong about that. This book was incredible and completely not what I was expecting. Plus, I had no idea how it was going to end and I love that! Even though it isn't heavy on description, it feels so alive and vivid. There are many parts of this book that have stayed with me. Definitely recommend this one.<br /><br /></span>

A boy that sees who you are but loves you. But you don't know who you are. I loved every surprise and discovery. Every time a lie came out I felt Jenna's pain but at the same time understood her parent's intentions. Such a difficult place this family was in. The ending was beautiful and sad and I couldn't help but tear up. Don't know if I want to read the next one because this one ended so perfectly and the next one will be different and not as good without Ethan. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Jenna Fox only has 10% of her original brain, "The Butterfly" her mom says. When Jenna wakes up from her coma she can't remember her life or why she lives in California now instead of Boston. Why none of her friends from her old life have called. Why her mom doesn't want her to go to school. Why she remembers history facts so easily. Why she isn't allowed to eat. Why her grandma doesn't seem to love her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_3290312228" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3290312228" />
    <a title="Cammie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4710682-cammie"><img alt="Cammie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577897159p2/4710682.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3290312228?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cammie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cammie" href="/user/show/4710682-cammie">Cammie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3290312228" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16134596271384031703">The Adoration of Jenna Fox explores how far a parent will go to save a child. Seventeen-year-old Jenna Fox is recovering from a terrible accident after spending over a year in a coma, and she remembers very little of her life. Slowly she remembers, and more about her life and the accident are revealed to the reader. The deception of Jenna's parents creates the major conflict of the story and drives the narrative.<br/>Mary E. Pearson said in an interview that she was inspired to write this story when </span>
  <span id="freeText16134596271384031703" style="display:none">The Adoration of Jenna Fox explores how far a parent will go to save a child. Seventeen-year-old Jenna Fox is recovering from a terrible accident after spending over a year in a coma, and she remembers very little of her life. Slowly she remembers, and more about her life and the accident are revealed to the reader. The deception of Jenna's parents creates the major conflict of the story and drives the narrative.<br />Mary E. Pearson said in an interview that she was inspired to write this story when her teen daughter was diagnosed with cancer. She spent much time in the hospital with her daughter, giving her much time to think and contemplate the world of medicine and medical ethics.<br />The Adoration of Jenna Fox is a futuristic medical dystopia but also seemed very realistic at times. The examination of medical ethics may have seemed unimaginable when the book was published in 2008, but just twelve years later, the issues in this YA novel don't seem that far fetched.<br />While this book is the first in a trilogy, I am not sure that I plan to read the other two books. The end of this one jumps ahead at the end to create enough conclusion for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16134596271384031703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6374017271200653761">I kept seeing rave reviews about this book - enough so that I couldn't resist getting a copy. I'm glad I did, b/c it was a great read and definitely one for my keepers shelf.<br/><br/>I really got into it. I found it to be pretty compelling for the most part and didn't even mind the science-y stuff :) I thought it was a very well thought out and presented premise and an original story. <br/><br/>The prose was just lovely to read and the way Pearson often varied it with verse style snippets was really kinda cool. <br/><br/>Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6374017271200653761" style="display:none">I kept seeing rave reviews about this book - enough so that I couldn't resist getting a copy. I'm glad I did, b/c it was a great read and definitely one for my keepers shelf.<br /><br />I really got into it. I found it to be pretty compelling for the most part and didn't even mind the science-y stuff :) I thought it was a very well thought out and presented premise and an original story. <br /><br />The prose was just lovely to read and the way Pearson often varied it with verse style snippets was really kinda cool. <br /><br />The characters all had their own flavour and most of them intrigued me. I would have liked to know a bit more about Dane and I found the parents to be a bit ambiguous, but it was from Jenna's POV - so I suppose it matches the direction the story was going in.<br /><br />I also found it refreshing to read a YA that didn't have a lot of edgy material or swear words in it. <br /><br />In particular, I really liked the ending. It was just different and I could really picture it and it gave the overall story that much more scope and impact. </span>

<div id="review_68867298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68867298" />
    <a title="Alana Kelly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2176822-alana-kelly"><img alt="Alana Kelly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456777827p2/2176822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68867298?book_show_action=true">Aug 25, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alana Kelly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alana Kelly" href="/user/show/2176822-alana-kelly">Alana Kelly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68867298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15616235926846684936">I’m having a hard time summing this book up into a tidy little paragraph because it has a little of everything. The story is set in the not-too-distant future and, as the summary says, follows Jenna Fox who has just awoken from a coma. But it’s also so much more then that. This book makes you stop and think about what it is that makes us who we are and if our humanity is limited by the cells in our body. It also takes a deep look at family and how perspective can make all the difference.<br/><br/>I have t</span>
  <span id="freeText15616235926846684936" style="display:none">I’m having a hard time summing this book up into a tidy little paragraph because it has a little of everything. The story is set in the not-too-distant future and, as the summary says, follows Jenna Fox who has just awoken from a coma. But it’s also so much more then that. This book makes you stop and think about what it is that makes us who we are and if our humanity is limited by the cells in our body. It also takes a deep look at family and how perspective can make all the difference.<br /><br />I have to say right off the bat I’m not very enamored with first person narratives. When they’re done well they’re great, but most of the time they fall flat for me. So when I say this book has one of the best first person narratives I’ve ever read, I really mean it. In fact, Jenna’s POV is what makes this story work. It lends a haunting sort of appeal to the story and I think everyone will relate to Jenna’s search for who she is. Some people will find the choppy narrative off putting, but I don't think it would have worked any other way.<br /><br />Throughout the book there were poems that often illuminated the internal struggle Jenna was going through and I found them to be exceptionally poignant. Example:<br /><br /> Pieces<br /> Isn’t that what all of life is anyway?<br /> Shards. Bits. Moments.<br /> Am I less because I have fewer, or do the few I have<br /> mean more?<br /> Am I just as full as anyone else? Enough?<br /> Pieces.<br /> Allys saying “I like you.”<br /> Gabriel snorting out bread, freeing me to laugh.<br /> And Ethan reminding me how much I do know.<br /> Pieces.<br /> I hold them like they are life itself.<br /> They nearly are.<br /><br />Pearson also included word definitions at the beginning of some of the chapters and I think it was a nice touch. I know it’s kind of disjointing, but language is such an important part of who we are as people that I feel like it just makes sense for Jenna to cling to that. Right away you can tell something is different about Jenna and it’s not too hard to guess what. But that’s not really the point of the story. Jenna’s journey to self-discovery is really the gem here.<br /><br />This book also brings up some interesting ideas about ethics in medicine and how the good thing and the right thing are far too often two much different things. I do think there were some issues left unresolved at the end of the book (like Dane) but I thought it was great overall. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15616235926846684936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6603759-misericordia-the-serendipity-aegis"><img alt="☘Misericordia☘ ~ The Serendipity Aegis ~  ⚡ϟ⚡ϟ⚡⛈ ✺❂❤❣" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585764390p2/6603759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4JhoV1cAT8KfeM+e5tLmfA3MbcmhDRJhKtsxideNz6hdWdTtddi2FNXvVTO0vTgBLCWOQGHy4oktH/HcZrZUBQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mANOcQfM62ZRzRZwe1qh5CUhyGmcxGueUt+KBE+Ho54lwvLLJRQSsBtajN0pNX+ZBMgr4Fw7m3ZVG0pR/rw4Mw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1154389913240057698">Mary E. Pearson is the NYT bestselling and award-winning author of eleven YA novels and one novella. Her works include the completed trilogy, <i>The Remnant Chronicles</i>, which in a starred review, Publisher’s Weekly called <i>“masterfully crafted.”</i> Her favorite activities as a child were climbing tall trees imagining she was a hero in some fantastical world, or running along fence tops and roofs pretendi</span>
  <span id="freeText1154389913240057698" style="display:none">Mary E. Pearson is the NYT bestselling and award-winning author of eleven YA novels and one novella. Her works include the completed trilogy, <i>The Remnant Chronicles</i>, which in a starred review, Publisher’s Weekly called <i>“masterfully crafted.”</i> Her favorite activities as a child were climbing tall trees imagining she was a hero in some fantastical world, or running along fence tops and roofs pretending she was a spy with a bagful of amazing gadgets. She was rarely herself. Amazingly, she never broke a bone until she caught a basketball in gym class. Catching real balls was not her forte. These days she continues to live in make-believe worlds she creates in her books. Her latest 2-book series, <i>Dance of Thieves</i>, allows her do all kinds of dangerous things without breaking any bones. So far. <br />You can learn more about Mary and her books at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.marypearson.com">www.marypearson.com</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1154389913240057698" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
